#METABOLOMICS WORKBENCH STUDY_ID:ST000259 ANALYSIS_ID:AN000411
VERSION             	1
CREATED_ON          	2016-09-17
#PROJECT
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	Effects of synthetic large-scale genome reduction on metabolism and metabolic
PR:PROJECT_TITLE                 	in a nutritionally complex environment
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	The soil bacterium Sinorhizobium meliloti forms nodules on the roots of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	plants, where N2 is reduced to ammonia. Its genome includes a 3.65 Mb
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	a 1.35 Mb pSymA megaplasmid, and a 1.68 Mb pSymB chromid. pSymA and pSymB
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	~45% of the genome and here a non-targeted approach was used to identify the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	consequences of the removal of these replicons. Polar and non-polar metabolites
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	wild-type, ?pSymA, ?pSymB, and ?pSymAB cells and supernatants across a growth
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	were analyzed by LC-HILIC-TOF-MS. 2008 metabolite features were identified in
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	extracellular metabolome of cells grown in LBmc containing yeast extract and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	hydrolysate. 1474 features were found from the intracellular metabolites of
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	grown in minimal M9-sucrose medium. Analysis revealed both time and genotype
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	the metabolome, with the removal of pSymB having a much greater effect than the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	of pSymA. Strains lacking pSymB showed an increase in sugar, amino acid, and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	metabolites in the intracellular metabolome, and the loss of pSymB clearly
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	the cell’s ability to catabolize exogenous amino acids. We conclude that
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	the ability of wild-type, ?pSymA, ?pSymB, and ?pSymAB strains to grow in both
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	and LBmc media, the removal of pSymA, and particularly pSymB, had clear and
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	effects on the S. meliloti metabolome. The larger effect associated with the
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	chromid is consistent with the large number of metabolic genes on this replicon
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	the greater genetic and metabolic integration of this replicon with the S.
PR:PROJECT_SUMMARY               	chromosome.
PR:INSTITUTE                     	McMaster University
PR:DEPARTMENT                    	Department of Biology
PR:LAST_NAME                     	Finan
PR:FIRST_NAME                    	Turlough
PR:ADDRESS                       	Department of Biology, McMaster University, Hamilton, Canada L8S4K1
PR:EMAIL                         	finan@mcmaster.ca
PR:PHONE                         	(+1)905-525-9140 ext 22932
#STUDY
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	metabolic contriubtion of pSymA and pSymB megaplasmid/chromid for multipartite
ST:STUDY_TITLE                   	meliloti cultured in rich LBmc medium
ST:STUDY_TYPE                    	megaplasmid deletion
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	We wished to evaluate the contribution of pSymA and pSymB towards the
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	of various metabolites in a nutritionally complex environment and to examine
ST:STUDY_SUMMARY                 	S. meliloti influences its surrounding environment.
ST:INSTITUTE                     	McMaster University
ST:DEPARTMENT                    	Department of Biology
